in Various Cities Across Iran\\\\n\\\\nA group of health care workers and nurses held a rally in front of the Majlis (parliament) building in Tehran, the capital of Iran, on Monday continuing their strike for the second consecutive day. They were protesting low wages and officials changing their employment classification. They also demanded their \xe2\x80\x9cspecial nursing bonus\xe2\x80\x9d to be paid for the contract nurses and workers. On Monday, pre-school teachers held a protest rally in front of the regime\xe2\x80\x99s Department of Education in the city of Izeh, Khuzestan province, demanding a change to their employment status. On Sunday, a large number of farmers from different cities went to Tehran and gathered in front of government entities and trade unions. The farmers were protesting the government purchasing their produce at low prices, which harms their revenue.\\\\n\\\\n\\\\nIran: Coronavirus Death Toll in 450 Cities Exceeds 117,200\\\\n\\\\nOver 117,200 people have died of the novel coronavirus in 450 cities checkered across all of Iran\xe2\x80\x99s 31 provinces, according to reports tallied by the Iranian opposition People\'s Mojahedin Organization of Iran as of Tuesday afternoon local time. The official death count declared by the regime stands at 27,419, around a fifth of the actual figure.\\\\n\xe2\x80\x9cWe are facing major difficulties regarding our ICU beds and hospitals where we can send patients to. Our medical personnel are also suffering from fatigue,\xe2\x80\x9d said Deputy Health Minister Iraj Harirchi on Tuesday. \xe2\x80\x9cIt has been seven to eight months that our workforce has been on duty with all its might. Some of our equipment are being overused beyond their capacity. Equipment such as CT scan devices, oxygen-concentrator units, and ventilators. This equipment, considering that they have been in use for some time, are wearing down and need service and maintenance. This is quite a challenging issue,\xe2\x80\x9d he added, according to the semi-official ISNA news agency.\\\\n\\\\n\\\\nDefiant Youths Target 6 Repressive Centers in Tehran and Other Cities\\\\n\\\\nIn the early hours of Monday in protest against the execution of detained protesters (Navid Afkari, and Mostafa Salehi), as well as the arrests and death sentences issued for arrested protesters, the defiant youths set fire on the entrances of six regime centers of repression in Tehran, and other cities.  At the same time, the defiant youths set fire to the banner of Qassem Soleimani and the banner of the Basij repressive forces in Tehran and Rasht, respectively.\\\\n\\\\nRead news in brief, October 7, 2020\\"},\\"description\\":{\\"simpleText\\":\\"Iran news in brief, October 7, 2020\\\\n\\\\nWorkers, Employees, and Nurses Protest in Various Cities Across Iran\\\\n\\\\nA group of health care workers and nurses held a rally in front of the Majlis (parliament) building in Tehran, the capital of Iran, on Monday continuing their strike for the second consecutive day. They were protesting low wages and officials changing their employment classification. They also demanded their \xe2\x80\x9cspecial nursing bonus\xe2\x80\x9d to be paid for the contract nurses and workers. On Monday, pre-school teachers held a protest rally in front of the regime\xe2\x80\x99s Department of Education in the city of Izeh, Khuzestan province, demanding a change to their employment status. On Sunday, a large number of farmers from different cities went to Tehran and gathered in front of government entities and trade unions. The farmers were protesting the government purchasing their produce at low prices, which harms their revenue.\\\\n\\\\n\\\\nIran: Coronavirus Death Toll in 450 Cities Exceeds 117,200\\\\n\\\\nOver 117,200 people have died of the novel coronavirus in 450 cities checkered across all of Iran\xe2\x80\x99s 31 provinces, according to reports tallied by the Iranian opposition People\'s Mojahedin Organization of Iran as of Tuesday afternoon local time. The official death count declared by the regime stands at 27,419, around a fifth of the actual figure.\\\\n\xe2\x80\x9cWe are facing major difficulties regarding our ICU beds and hospitals where we can send patients to. Our medical personnel are also suffering from fatigue,\xe2\x80\x9d said Deputy Health Minister Iraj Harirchi on Tuesday. \xe2\x80\x9cIt has been seven to eight months that our workforce has been on duty with all its might. Some of our equipment are being overused beyond their capacity. Equipment such as CT scan devices, oxygen-concentrator units, and ventilators. This equipment, considering that they have been in use for some time, are wearing down and need service and maintenance. This is quite a challenging issue,\xe2\x80\x9d he added, according to the semi-official ISNA news agency.\\\\n\\\\n\\\\nDefiant Youths Target 6 Repressive Centers in Tehran and Other Cities\\\\n\\\\nIn the early hours of Monday in protest against the execution of detained protesters (Navid Afkari, and Mostafa Salehi), as well as the arrests and death sentences issued for arrested protesters, the defiant youths set fire on the entrances of six regime centers of repression in Tehran, and other cities.  At the same time, the defiant youths set fire to the banner of Qassem Soleimani and the banner of the Basij repressive forces in Tehran and Rasht, respectively.\\\\n\\\\nRead news in brief, October 7, 2020\\n\\nWorkers, Employees, and Nurses Protest in Various Cities Across Iran\\n\\nA group of health care workers and nurses held a rally in front of the Majlis (parliament) building in Tehran, the capital of Iran, on Monday continuing their strike for the second consecutive day. They were protesting low wages and officials changing their employment classification. They also demanded their \xe2\x80\x9cspecial nursing bonus\xe2\x80\x9d to be paid for the contract nurses and workers. On Monday, pre-school teachers held a protest rally in front of the regime\xe2\x80\x99s Department of Education in the city of Izeh, Khuzestan province, demanding a change to their employment status. On Sunday, a large number of farmers from different cities went to Tehran and gathered in front of government entities and trade unions. The farmers were protesting the government purchasing their produce at low prices, which harms their revenue.\\n\\n\\nIran: Coronavirus Death Toll in 450 Cities Exceeds 117,200\\n\\nOver 117,200 people have died of the novel coronavirus in 450 cities checkered across all of Iran\xe2\x80\x99s 31 provinces, according to reports tallied by the Iranian opposition People\'s Mojahedin Organization of Iran as of Tuesday afternoon local time. The official death count declared by the regime stands at 27,419, around a fifth of the actual figure.\\n\xe2\x80\x9cWe are facing major difficulties regarding our ICU beds and hospitals where we can send patients to. Our medical personnel are also suffering from fatigue,\xe2\x80\x9d said Deputy Health Minister Iraj Harirchi on Tuesday. \xe2\x80\x9cIt has been seven to eight months that our workforce has been on duty with all its might. workers and nurses held a rally in front of the Majlis (parliament) building in Tehran, the capital of Iran, on Monday continuing their strike for the second consecutive day. They were protesting low wages and officials changing their employment classification. They also demanded their \xe2\x80\x9cspecial nursing bonus\xe2\x80\x9d to be paid for the contract nurses and workers. On Monday, pre-school teachers held a protest rally in front of the regime\xe2\x80\x99s Department of Education in the city of Izeh, Khuzestan province, demanding a change to their employment status. On Sunday, a large number of farmers from different cities went to Tehran and gathered in front of government entities and trade unions. The farmers were protesting the government purchasing their produce at low prices, which harms their revenue.\\n\\n\\nIran: Coronavirus Death Toll in 450 Cities Exceeds 117,200\\n\\nOver 117,200 people have died of the novel coronavirus in 450 cities checkered across all of Iran\xe2\x80\x99s 31 provinces, according to reports tallied by the Iranian opposition People\'s Mojahedin Organization of Iran as of Tuesday afternoon local time. The official death count declared by the regime stands at 27,419, around a fifth of the actual figure.\\n\xe2\x80\x9cWe are facing major difficulties regarding our ICU beds and hospitals where we can send patients to. Our medical personnel are also suffering from fatigue,\xe2\x80\x9d said Deputy Health Minister Iraj Harirchi on Tuesday. \xe2\x80\x9cIt has been seven to eight months that our workforce has been on duty with all its might. Some of our equipment are being overused beyond their capacity. Equipment such as CT scan devices, oxygen-concentrator units, and ventilators. This equipment, considering that they have been in use for some time, are wearing down and need service and maintenance. This is quite a challenging issue,\xe2\x80\x9d he added, according to the semi-official ISNA news agency.\\n\\n\\nDefiant Youths Target 6 Repressive Centers in Tehran and Other Cities\\n\\nIn the early hours of Monday in protest against the execution of detained protesters (Navid Afkari, and Mostafa Salehi), as well as the arrests and death sentences issued for arrested protesters, the defiant youths set fire on the entrances of six regime centers of repression in Tehran, and other cities.  At the same time, the defiant youths set fire to the banner of Qassem Soleimani and the banner of the Basij repressive forces in Tehran and Rasht, respectively.\\n\\nRead
